    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9391019833204519108"><i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> not only debuted the talent of best-selling novelist Ira Levin to rave reviews, it also set a new standard in the art of mystery and suspense. Now a modern classic, as gripping in its tautly plotted action as it is penetrating in its exploration of a criminal mind, it tells the shocking tale of a young man who will stop at nothing--not even murder--to g</span>
  <span id="freeText9391019833204519108" style="display:none"><i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> not only debuted the talent of best-selling novelist Ira Levin to rave reviews, it also set a new standard in the art of mystery and suspense. Now a modern classic, as gripping in its tautly plotted action as it is penetrating in its exploration of a criminal mind, it tells the shocking tale of a young man who will stop at nothing--not even murder--to get where he wants to go. For he has dreams; plans. He also has charm, good looks, sex appeal, intelligence. And he has a problem. Her name is Dorothy; she loves him, and she's pregnant. The solution may demand desperate measures. But, then, he looks like the kind of guy who could get away with murder. Compellingly, step by determined step, the novel follows this young man in his execution of one plan he had neither dreamed nor foreseen. Nor does he foresee how inexorably he will be enmeshed in the consequences of his own extreme deed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9391019833204519108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_24952092').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_24952092').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_24952092').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    . sister did not talk the way the letter was written<br />. Anomalies in the Dories attire led Ellen to the conclusion she was planning to get married that <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    . sister did not talk the way the letter was written<br />. Anomalies in the Dories attire led Ellen to the conclusion she was planning to get married that day<br /> - sister would not wear that blouse with that suit (something old)<br /> - sister bought gloves when she already had some (something new)<br /> - sister borrowed belt unnecessarily (something borrowed)<br /> - sister was carrying a turquoise blue handkerchief which did not <br /> match her outfit (something blue)<br />. <br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_2201731965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2201731965" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2201731965?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780762102518" href="/book/show/2396316.A_Kiss_Before_Dying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=greed">greed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=hardboiled">hardboiled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=book-to-film">book-to-film</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2201731965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16725854268952115511"><b>”’You’re crazy,’ he told himself aloud one day, looking at the list. ‘You’re a crazy nut,’ he said affectionately. He didn’t really think that; he thought he was daring, audacious, brilliant, intrepid and bold.”</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/A20Kiss20Before20Dying_zpslcxemmkx.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534215510i/26124853.jpg' alt=' photo A20Kiss20Before20Dying_zpslcxemmkx.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>1956 movie version of the book. I remember it being really good.</b><br/><br/>I can’t even tell you his name because he didn’t tell me until I was a ⅓ of the way through the novel. I thought I knew who he was, but I was wrong. You will be wrong, too, and I want you to be wrong because I want you to</span>
  <span id="freeText16725854268952115511" style="display:none"><b>”’You’re crazy,’ he told himself aloud one day, looking at the list. ‘You’re a crazy nut,’ he said affectionately. He didn’t really think that; he thought he was daring, audacious, brilliant, intrepid and bold.”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/A20Kiss20Before20Dying_zpslcxemmkx.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534215510i/26124853.jpg" alt=" photo A20Kiss20Before20Dying_zpslcxemmkx.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>1956 movie version of the book. I remember it being really good.</b><br><br>I can’t even tell you his name because he didn’t tell me until I was a ⅓ of the way through the novel. I thought I knew who he was, but I was wrong. You will be wrong, too, and I want you to be wrong because I want you to be as unnerved as I was when you find out who he is. More importantly, you will discover what he is. <br><br><b>He is a sociopath.</b><br><br>He tries to fit into society but finds the experience very unsatisfying. <i>”By the end of August, when he had been in New York five months and had had six jobs, he was again prey to the awful insecurity of being one among many rather than one alone; unadmired and with no tangible sign of success. He sat in his furnished room and devoted some time to serious self-analysis. If he had not found what he wanted in these six jobs, he decided, it was unlikely that he would find it in the next six.”</i><br><br>So our guy can’t find the perfect job and decides that getting rich on his own (he is so brilliant he should be rich) is a lot more work, takes a lot of time and a dollop of luck. Wouldn’t it be easier to just marry money? Hey, you don’t have to be a sociopath to think that is a good idea. After weighing all the girls at college, he finally settles on Dorothy Kingship. Her name denotes her status. Her father is a copper king worth fabulous amounts of money. She is the middle daughter of three. She is beautiful (bonus) and insecure (huge bonus). Everything is going smoothly; then Dorothy gets knocked up. <br><br>He has already jumped from the highboard into the family pool, but instead of a swan dive, he smacks the water with that ugly sound of a dive gone wrong. All those puffy cloud dreams he had about his future as the son-in-law of a filthy, rich man dissipate, and all he is left with is the vision of Dorothy’s swelling stomach. <br><br><b>This can’t be!</b><br><br>Her father will disown her. Dorothy doesn’t care about the money, which is infuriating to him. Their conversation reminds me of the interactions between William and Jocelyn in the movie <i>A Knight’s Tale</i>. <br><br><b>”Jocelyn: ‘Now be gone! Go! William.’<br><br>William: ‘Where will we live? In my hovel? With the pigs inside during the winter so they won't freeze?’<br><br>Joceyln: ‘Yes, William. With the pigs.’”</b><br><br>Which is all very romantic...for about a week, and then when her hair, clothes, and skin start to smell like swine, she will pine for the scents of jasmine, lavender, and rose. <br><br>He makes that argument to Dorothy, but really he isn’t worried about how she will react to not having the money. He is frantically trying hang onto his dreams of the Kingship fortune. Without all that money, Dorothy is just a nice girl. <br><br>This is where the sociopath segment of the book takes off. The decisions he makes to fix this issue are, frankly, ruthless. He isn’t worried about the morality of it, but he is worried about getting caught and facing punishment. <br><br>This is bad; this is very bad, but the moment when my stomach does a few unnatural flip flops is when it occurs to him that it is going to be easier to seduce another Kingship daughter than it is to start all over researching and romancing another debutante. <br><br>Next up, Ellen.<br><br>And if Ellen doesn’t work out, there is always Marion.<br><br><b>*SHUDDER!!*</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/A20Kiss20Before20Dying201991_zps6orztgvh.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534215510i/26124854._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo A20Kiss20Before20Dying201991_zps6orztgvh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>There was also a 1991 film version of the book, starring Sean Young and Matt Dillon, that I have not seen but from what I read deviates significantly away from the original plot.</b><br><br>Ira Levin does such a wonderful job creating so much unease in the reader. The tension continues to grow with each turned page, and I found myself rooting against this guy, but at the same time, I was still fascinated to see what he was going to do next. Will he be stopped? And at what point will he make that fatal error? It was no surprise to me to discover that Levin won the 1954 Edgar Award for best first novel. He was twenty-four years old when he wrote this book, but his youth is never evident in the plotting or in the character development. It reads like a writer working in his prime. <br><br>I want to share this moment when the criminal mind is accessing the books owned by one of his potential victims and what those books say about her: <i>”...and the books, for what better index of the personality is there?---(the novels and plays, the non-fiction and verse, all chosen in proportion and representation of her tastes). It was like the concentrated abbreviation of a Help Wanted ad. The egocentricity which motivated it was not that of the spoiled, but of the too little spoiled; the lonely.”</i><br><br>Hey buddy, I don’t know what you’d make of my library, expect that maybe I needed to see a shrink, but I can tell you this reader is never lonely as long as I have a book close to hand. <br><br>Highly recommended for those who like their books hardboiled in salt and vinegar. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16725854268952115511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14098945235300048697" style="display:none">I have loved Ira Levin ever since I watched a movie in 1982 -Deathtrap- based on his 1978 play. It is a must see for mystery lovers, and A KISS BEFORE DYING- Levin's first novel -written in 1953- is a must read!<br><br>The story starts out like many stories do...<br><br>Poor boy<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398641075i/9444767.gif" alt=" photo fd2563e8-70fe-4a76-9c8d-51f70f4f751c_zps1a1636ac.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>meets-<br><br>Rich girl<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398640811i/9444740.jpg" alt=" photo 543e29b3-1245-43b7-8c63-c27587629afd_zps72cbeba1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Poor boy and rich girl start dating<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398634504i/9444064.png" alt=" photo 6806cd21-85c5-45a0-8b81-b9a8e9de41a7_zpseda9e308.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rich girl gets pregnant<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398634504i/9444065.png" alt=" photo 3748e74f-0886-4fb1-8f8b-1a2c9a321b2a_zps4be20bf8.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...and this is where things get a little interesting-<br><br>Poor boy- is actually a psychopath- only dating rich girl so he could marry her for her money. She is a naive girl from a wealthy family, and meets the man she thinks she wants to marry while studying at Stoddard College- in Blue River, Iowa. Things with Dorothy and her new beau are going perfectly until she announces she is pregnant, and instead of walking down the aisle- she is falling to her death. The police rule it a suicide, but her sister Ellen isn't buying it, and goes to Blue River in search of the truth. <br><br>A KISS BEFORE DYING is a suspenseful well-plotted mystery- where one never knows who to trust.</span>

<div id="review_3231659399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3231659399" />
    <a title="David Putnam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam"><img alt="David Putnam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372638034p2/5463364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3231659399?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Putnam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Putnam" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam">David Putnam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3231659399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14423864625799214411">Here’s one that really surprised me. I had not expected to like this one as much. And it is also one I don’t know how I had missed for so long. I came across this title because an author I highly respect talked about the book and how it had influenced his writing career--novels (along with Ruth Rendell’s One Across, Two Down—which is now also on the TBR pile). This book is written in the 50’s-60’s style with more narrative “telling” than showing but the author is highly skilled and pulls it off.</span>
  <span id="freeText14423864625799214411" style="display:none">Here’s one that really surprised me. I had not expected to like this one as much. And it is also one I don’t know how I had missed for so long. I came across this title because an author I highly respect talked about the book and how it had influenced his writing career--novels (along with Ruth Rendell’s One Across, Two Down—which is now also on the TBR pile). This book is written in the 50’s-60’s style with more narrative “telling” than showing but the author is highly skilled and pulls it off. I picked this book up started reading and couldn’t put it down. The point of view character is despicable, (like the one in The Talented Mr. Ripley by Highsmith) and yet the author kept me engage the entire time. It was like watching a slow-motion train wreck. I knew what was going to happen and couldn’t look away. For those readers who like this kind of suspense, I highly recommend this book.<br />David Putnam author of The Bruno Johnson series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14423864625799214411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_860278047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/860278047" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_2629369658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629369658" />
    <a title="Marwan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49765318-marwan"><img alt="Marwan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472047723p2/49765318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2629369658?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marwan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marwan" href="/user/show/49765318-marwan">Marwan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849015912" href="/book/show/12279023-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629369658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8094314585785687286">Stephen King has described Ira Levin as <b>" the Swiss watchmaker of the suspense novel"</b> and I couldn't agree more. <b>Rosemary's Baby</b> was great, but this one was a masterpiece, truly a masterpiece. A plot filled with twists that makes you so anxious to read more, thinking about it even when you're not reading. <br/><br/>I can't say much about the novel without spoiling it. But <b>"Saving the best for last"</b> is one way describe it, and I recommend it to anyone who likes psychological suspense. <br/><br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14981581303177444262">Thank you, thank you, thank you to my friend Delee, who recommended this humdinger of a novel. Ira Levin, best known for his terrifying <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228296.Rosemary_s_Baby' title='Rosemary's Baby by Ira Levin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rosemary's Baby</a>, wrote <i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> as his first novel. The novel won the 1954 Edgar Award for Best First Novel, and readers will marvel that this suspense-filled thrill ride of a book could possibly have been written by a first-time novelist, one just 24 years old.<br/><br/>Levin packs surprise after surprise into this novel, a book that will leave you exhausted w</span>
  <span id="freeText14981581303177444262" style="display:none">Thank you, thank you, thank you to my friend Delee, who recommended this humdinger of a novel. Ira Levin, best known for his terrifying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228296.Rosemary_s_Baby" title="Rosemary's Baby by Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary's Baby</a>, wrote <i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> as his first novel. The novel won the 1954 Edgar Award for Best First Novel, and readers will marvel that this suspense-filled thrill ride of a book could possibly have been written by a first-time novelist, one just 24 years old.<br /><br />Levin packs surprise after surprise into this novel, a book that will leave you exhausted when you release the breath you hadn’t realized you were holding. Highly recommended.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954777859" />

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11458998-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1923002-mara?shelf=thrill-me">thrill-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1923002-mara?shelf=codename-duchess">codename-duchess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1923002-mara?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954777859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14704899101974989370">If <a title='A Kiss Before Dying' href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11458998-a-kiss-before-dying' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>
    <strong>A Kiss Before Dying</strong>
  </em>
</a><strong> </strong>were to come out tomorrow, I might use words like "predictable" to describe certain aspects of it. However, <a title='Ira Levin' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ira Levin</a> published this (his first novel) in 1954, which gives it the sort of satisfying, but olden-timey thrill I remember getting from watching the likes of <em>Double Indemnity</em> and <em>Wait Until Dark</em> in my grandparents' home as a kid. <br/> <br/>There's something different about witnessing 50s characters unwittingly fall prey to the machinations of a seemingly swell g</span>
  <span id="freeText14704899101974989370" style="display:none">If <a title="A Kiss Before Dying" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11458998-a-kiss-before-dying" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>
    <strong>A Kiss Before Dying</strong>
  </em>
</a><strong> </strong>were to come out tomorrow, I might use words like "predictable" to describe certain aspects of it. However, <a title="Ira Levin" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ira Levin</a> published this (his first novel) in 1954, which gives it the sort of satisfying, but olden-timey thrill I remember getting from watching the likes of <em>Double Indemnity</em> and <em>Wait Until Dark</em> in my grandparents' home as a kid. <br> <br>There's something different about witnessing 50s characters unwittingly fall prey to the machinations of a seemingly swell guy. After all, not having been subjected to endless hours of crime procedural television, and without Google, those prone to trust don’t come across as cloyingly naïve.<br> <br>There's plenty of suspense and dread packing into a worthwhile, brief and classic mystery.<br> <br>Also, for the purposes of disambiguation, <em>A Kiss Before Dying</em> is not to be confused with <a title="A Kiss While Dying Archer 502" href="http://archer.wikia.com/wiki/Archer_Vice:_A_Kiss_While_Dying" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>
    <strong>A Kiss While Dying</strong>
  </em>
</a><strong> </strong>which, of course, looks something like this.<br> <br><a title="A Kiss While Dying" href="http://imgur.com/zhHVh2O" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401760098ra/9843841.gif" alt="A Kiss While Dying" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4103086327298102392">If that new thriller in your hand is unsatisfying or disappointing, put it down. Get this one.   <span id="freeText4103086327298102392" style="display:none">If that new thriller in your hand is unsatisfying or disappointing, put it down. Get this one. Trust me.<br /><br />A handsome and smoothtalking gold digger has a plan. He will stop at nothing to get what he wants, even murder. <br /><br />One of the best books I have read this year! This mystery / suspense / thriller / crime novel was amazing! This 1953 modern classic set the bar of what the current thriller genre authors are *trying* so hard to do. It has aged well and is an easy and engrossing read. I stress "engrossing." I managed to wiggle out of some house chores today to finish this one. <br /><br />Levin is also the author of "Rosemary's Baby" and "The Stepford Wives" but this one is a million times better, in my opinion. This one sucks you in and won't let you go, it has twists, turns, it has it all! My heart was racing at the climatic ending. I highly recommend and feel it is a must read. This novel has been made into a movie twice, the first movie starring Robert Wagner and the second starring Matt Dillon.  So, if it is good enough to be made into a movie twice, you know it has to be good. <br /><br />*** One word of caution: some harsh profanity. Not on every page and not in every chapter, but it has one particular harsh expletive (that I hate) around 10 times in the entire novel.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1144813107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144813107" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144813107?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/20878687-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">gold-digging sociopaths, rich girls with single sisters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=modern-classic">modern-classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=rich-people">rich-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=sociopaths">sociopaths</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=anti-heroes">anti-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=1950s">1950s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144813107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12567146668516222607">If at first you don't succeed, get rid of the bitch and move on to the next sister.<br/><br/><i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> is a taut little thriller about a sociopath who conceives an ingenuous plan to seduce the daughter of a wealthy copper baron. Except she goes and gets pregnant before his plan can come to fruition. Since Daddy is the moralistic disinheriting type, he figures a kid before they are properly married and he's had time to work his charms and soften the old man up will just ruin everything. When he c</span>
  <span id="freeText12567146668516222607" style="display:none">If at first you don't succeed, get rid of the bitch and move on to the next sister.<br /><br /><i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> is a taut little thriller about a sociopath who conceives an ingenuous plan to seduce the daughter of a wealthy copper baron. Except she goes and gets pregnant before his plan can come to fruition. Since Daddy is the moralistic disinheriting type, he figures a kid before they are properly married and he's had time to work his charms and soften the old man up will just ruin everything. When he can't persuade her to get rid of it, he's left with only one option - a well-planned murder in which he manages to make it look like a suicide, and then avoid any connection between him and the dead girl.<br /><br />Which allows him to move on to daughter #2.<br /><br />But daughter #2 proves a little too intuitive — she starts putting clues together and realizing her sister didn't commit suicide, and wants to find out who murdered her. She figures everything out just a little too late.<br /><br />And our boy, as long on audacity as he is short on scruples, decides third time's the charm: the rich industrialist had <em>three</em> daughters, and after all that research he did to seduce the first two, he knows the oldest sister pretty well...<br /><br />As improbable as this story may sound, I couldn't really spot any plot holes. Sure, our protagonist needed a bit of luck here and there, but nothing so overwhelmingly coincidental as to be completely implausible. He's just a meticulous, cold-blooded schemer with a knack for manipulation.<br /><br />A lot of people want books with "relatable" protagonists. Well, the protagonist of this book is a murderous, gold-digging sociopath. You want him to trip up and get caught, and you want his victims to get away, and at the same time, the exciting part is finding out how he's going to get away with it.<br /><br />This book is dated now — it was written in 1954 and it's set in the early fifties, so the campus life described, and the so-visible class distinctions are not the same now, but that just makes this suspenseful novel a period piece as well. In fact, some of the period details are what made it interesting. For example, there is surprisingly little moralizing about the proposed abortion — she doesn't want to do it, but it seems more for emotional reasons than any real ethical or religious qualms. And it struck me that in some ways, the "boy from the wrong side of the tracks" was a thing that would be even harder to envision today — nowadays, we like to pretend that American society is less class-stratified, but that's because the rich are increasingly distant and out of sight. Working class people just don't socialize, at all, with the very wealthy, which makes it easier for us to pretend that there is no such thing as class.<br /><br />Ira Levin also wrote other thrillers, like <i>Rosemary's Baby</i> and <i>The Stepford Wives</i>, and with this pacey, suspenseful novel, it's easy to see how readily his stories became a part of pop culture. Definitely worth reading, and motivated me to read more by him someday.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12567146668516222607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3252084828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5358082880364757892">Between 1948 & 1954 legendary film director & master of suspense Alfred Hitchcock supplied us with unbearable tension in films like Rope, Strangers on a Train & Rear Window. Then in 1954 a 24 year old writer called Ira Levin published his first novel, A Kiss Before Dying, & added a new dimension to the word suspense.<br/>I've always felt that Levin's tale of murder & menace worked far better than either of the film adaptations. Perhaps Hitchcock could have made a better version ? It's been a long tim</span>
  <span id="freeText5358082880364757892" style="display:none">Between 1948 &amp; 1954 legendary film director &amp; master of suspense Alfred Hitchcock supplied us with unbearable tension in films like Rope, Strangers on a Train &amp; Rear Window. Then in 1954 a 24 year old writer called Ira Levin published his first novel, A Kiss Before Dying, &amp; added a new dimension to the word suspense.<br />I've always felt that Levin's tale of murder &amp; menace worked far better than either of the film adaptations. Perhaps Hitchcock could have made a better version ? It's been a long time since I first read this novel, which did have one advantage: I could remember who wasn't the killer, but I was damned if I could remember who it was!<br />Though not my favourite Levin novel, it's an impressive debut &amp; one that was well worth a second read.</span>

<div id="review_947290699" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947290699" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781605981833" href="/book/show/9865673-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947290699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12897766265549863214">Those of you who have followed my reviewing adventures for a while may have noticed a downward rating trend when it comes to Ira Levin's work. <br/><br/>Rosemary's Baby, read in 2011 - 5 stars<br/>The Stepford Wives, read in 2013 - 4 stars<br/>Sliver, read in 2015 - 1 star<br/><br/>Now, thankfully, I can say that the trend is back on the upswing! Not that it could have gone any lower, honestly. Sliver was TERRIBLE. It would be super hard to get worse than that. <br/><br/>So, I am pretty pleasantly surprised that I enjoyed this book as</span>
  <span id="freeText12897766265549863214" style="display:none">Those of you who have followed my reviewing adventures for a while may have noticed a downward rating trend when it comes to Ira Levin's work. <br /><br />Rosemary's Baby, read in 2011 - 5 stars<br />The Stepford Wives, read in 2013 - 4 stars<br />Sliver, read in 2015 - 1 star<br /><br />Now, thankfully, I can say that the trend is back on the upswing! Not that it could have gone any lower, honestly. Sliver was TERRIBLE. It would be super hard to get worse than that. <br /><br />So, I am pretty pleasantly surprised that I enjoyed this book as much as I did. I picked this up on Audible in 2014 (the year BEFORE the awful-terrible-bad Sliver), and then never got around to reading it, because that's what I do. But then after reading Sliver, I was honestly a little afraid that the bloom was off the Ira Levin rose for me and there was no coming back from that. <br /><br />I can't say that this book was anywhere near the Rosemary's Baby level of good, but it WAS pretty good, considering that it was Levin's debut novel, and I'll be honest and say that there was a twist in the middle that had me all like "WHUT? O_O" I did not see it coming AT ALL, and it's probably one of the best twists I've seen in a long time. <br /><br />I will say that some of the early 50s attitudes toward women came across as maddeningly sexist, but... it was a different time then. There were ALSO moments of female empowerment, to be fair, though not in any vital or important way to the story. And the outcomes usually favored or featured men. <br /><br />Anyway, I liked this well enough to think that maybe the rest of Levin's work isn't a complete loss to me after Sliver, but I don't really have too much to say. It is a bit dated, but in a "this aged well" kind of way rather than a "old and sad" kind of way. <br /><br />One note on the audiobook... I'm not a fan of readers who try too hard to "do the voices", and this reader did that for one of the characters, to a really distracting and annoying degree, even though the voice wasn't caricaturish or anything. There's a character that is a DJ on the local college radio station, and he is described as having a smooth, announcer type voice. Totally legit for a DJ, but this is ALSO a college kid. So he should NOT sound like a modern day George Takei. Which is exactly what he sounded like to me. And it was annoying. <br /><br />Otherwise, no complaints from the audio. Or the book, really. Pretty solidly good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12897766265549863214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_308889174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308889174" />
    <a title="Joanne Sheppard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7682048-joanne-sheppard"><img alt="Joanne Sheppard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412719438p2/7682048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308889174?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne Sheppard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne Sheppard" href="/user/show/7682048-joanne-sheppard">Joanne Sheppard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849015912" href="/book/show/12279023-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308889174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7088190630744206357">The title 'A Kiss Before Dying' conjures up, for me, an image of a 1950s pulp thriller with a fabulous, stylish cover featuring a woman who looks like the hourglassy one from Mad Men and a man in a fedora concealing a gun. And indeed, that's pretty much exactly what A Kiss Before Dying is, on the face of it - it's a crime novel published in 1953 about a handsome psychopath who preys upon a series of rich young women in a bid to secure a stake in their father's fortune.<br/><br/>And yet, while A Kiss Befor</span>
  <span id="freeText7088190630744206357" style="display:none">The title 'A Kiss Before Dying' conjures up, for me, an image of a 1950s pulp thriller with a fabulous, stylish cover featuring a woman who looks like the hourglassy one from Mad Men and a man in a fedora concealing a gun. And indeed, that's pretty much exactly what A Kiss Before Dying is, on the face of it - it's a crime novel published in 1953 about a handsome psychopath who preys upon a series of rich young women in a bid to secure a stake in their father's fortune.<br /><br />And yet, while A Kiss Before Dying, by the late Ira Levin, has all the signature style and undeniable glamour of a somewhat noirish American thriller, not to mention a characteristically sensationalist plot, there's plenty to set it apart.<br /><br />The story begins with an unnamed young man plotting the death of his fiancée, Dorothy Kingship - a pretty, rich, naive college student. Having planned to marry her to get his hands on some of her father's money, he's furious to learn that she's pregnant. This being somewhere around 1950, this seems likely to force them to marry immediately and incur the wrath of Dorothy's father, who will almost certainly disinherit her as a result, leaving the nameless protagonist poorer than ever and saddled with a wife and child he never wanted as well as ruining his master-plan. Consequently, when pills from a backstreet abortionist fail to work their magic, the only alternative, he feels, is murder.<br /><br />It's chilling, tense and (like the much-maligned and underrated 1950s shocker, Peyton Place) remarkably evocative of its time and setting. And it's a decent enough thriller plot, of course. All pretty straightforward...<br /><br />But then, Levin pulls a particularly clever trick. He switches the novel's point of view. Suddenly, we're in the position of Ellen Kingship, trying to discover who has wronged her younger sister. All she knows is that she has to look for a handsome, charming blond college boy in his mid-20s (his academic career having been interrupted by World War II, of course). There are a number of contenders. And it could be any of them. Terrifyingly, any of these affable, bright, all-American boys Ellen meets could have the mind of a psychopathic killer - a mind into which we, as readers, already have a horrific insight.<br /><br />Those familiar with Ira Levin's best-known works - Rosemary's Baby, The Boys From Brazil, The Stepford Wives, all of which became immensely successful films - will know that his books tend to stretch plausibility a little, and yes, A Kiss Before Dying does this too. But somehow, it's all so neatly plotted in every detail, with every character so absolutely spot-on for the roles they have to play in the story, that I found myself believing every word. It may be pulp-influenced at times, and at times it's a wee bit overblown, but the writing is so sharp that it simply doesn't matter, and Levin has been astute in building his characters convincingly to give them credible motivation.<br /><br />As in his other books that I mentioned, Levin uses A Kiss Before Dying to tug at a sinister, dysfunctional thread that unravels the fragile tapestry of a classic American setting to reveal a dark, calculating cruelty lying beneath. Nobody and nothing are what they seem in Levin's novels, and reading this book is like stepping into the world of a stylish Hitchcock film full of beautiful women, fabulous outfits, ever-building tension, surprise plot twists and ambiguously charming men who may or may not be calculating killers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7088190630744206357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1849333139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1849333139" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7891507-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443344607p2/7891507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1849333139?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/7891507-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1849333139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12298885953765825016">It always amazes me how many people have never heard of Ira Levin. "Ira who? Never heard of him". "You saw the movie The Stepford Wives or Rosemary's Baby? Well, Levin wrote those". Yup, everyone saw those movies but still they don't recognize Levin's name. It's a shame really because he was a brilliant writer with an amazing gift at storytelling. In fact, A Kiss Before Dying was his first and it won an award. It was written over six decades ago but it's an easy to read. Not nearly as dated as y</span>
  <span id="freeText12298885953765825016" style="display:none">It always amazes me how many people have never heard of Ira Levin. "Ira who? Never heard of him". "You saw the movie The Stepford Wives or Rosemary's Baby? Well, Levin wrote those". Yup, everyone saw those movies but still they don't recognize Levin's name. It's a shame really because he was a brilliant writer with an amazing gift at storytelling. In fact, A Kiss Before Dying was his first and it won an award. It was written over six decades ago but it's an easy to read. Not nearly as dated as you'd think.<br /><br />It's kind of the opposite of a murdery-mystery. You know who did the murder because you're actually following him and his plans. At least for the first one. The plot thickens (as they say) and the murderer gets deeper and deeper into the hole he dug for himself. The thing I really liked, once I realized it, was that the murderer's name isn't mentioned once for about half the book. Once details start being looked at and suspects named, you're just as much in the dark as the characters trying to capture him. <br /><br />I recommend reading Levin in general, he's that good, but this is a great place to start.<br />Levin was a genius. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12298885953765825016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1393703011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1393703011" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1393703011?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/20878687-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393703011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14892312743409513659">I'm going to mention that when you read this you will undoubtedly (well unless you've just started reading books or watching movies and TV...or I suppose have been in a long coma) have come across the idea, the plot, even the characters before. It would not be fair to hold that against the book however because the book was written in 1953 and probably originated many of what are now stereotypical ingredients to some thrillers.<br/><br/>If you can "let the book" or if you really aren't familiar with books,</span>
  <span id="freeText14892312743409513659" style="display:none">I'm going to mention that when you read this you will undoubtedly (well unless you've just started reading books or watching movies and TV...or I suppose have been in a long coma) have come across the idea, the plot, even the characters before. It would not be fair to hold that against the book however because the book was written in 1953 and probably originated many of what are now stereotypical ingredients to some thrillers.<br /><br />If you can "let the book" or if you really aren't familiar with books, movies, TV program etc. similar this book will hang you out with an odd since of suspense mixed with that terrible certainty of impending doom. I must say that while I pretty much saw it all coming (again not the book's fault it has been copied over and over) it is still obvious that this was masterfully written.<br /><br />I read one reviewer who said he couldn't help but sort of like our psychopathic (or possibly sociopathic) protagonist. I never got there. I did "sort of" start to see inside his head and his life. Levin while not actually trying to explain Bud's mind (and emotions) did give us a little insight at least into his background and where he came from. maybe some insight into what Ira Levin thinks. Psychopathy and sociopathy are things I've wondered about before. Why do some people completely lack empathy? Why do some have almost no emotion, fear or caring? Why do some see others people as only "things" to be used and manipulated?<br /><br />I don't know but their existence is in fact horrifying. <br /><br />The (almost inevitable) climatic conclusion <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and Bud's circular experience <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are well handled and more realistic than idealized, softened or explained. It simply "is". Like life.<br /><br />I can recommend this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14892312743409513659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3416566612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3416566612" />
    <a title="Nigeyb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10301421-nigeyb"><img alt="Nigeyb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593065725p2/10301421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3416566612?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigeyb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigeyb" href="/user/show/10301421-nigeyb">Nigeyb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849015912" href="/book/show/12279023-a-kiss-before-dying">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3416566612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16923834575100254348">A friend recommended <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin' title='Ira Levin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ira Levin</a>. He wrote only seven novels, but they included one that prompted the gothic revival, Rosemary's Baby, as well as The Stepford Wives, The Boys from Brazil and Sliver, all of which were made into films. Along with these he also wrote the long-running Broadway comic thriller Deathtrap. All of which makes me wonder why I’d left it so long to sample his work.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12279023.A_Kiss_Before_Dying' title='A Kiss Before Dying by Ira Levin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Kiss Before Dying</a> (1953), his first novel, is a taut and tense suspense novel. It reminded me of Patricia Highs</span>
  <span id="freeText16923834575100254348" style="display:none">A friend recommended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin" title="Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ira Levin</a>. He wrote only seven novels, but they included one that prompted the gothic revival, Rosemary's Baby, as well as The Stepford Wives, The Boys from Brazil and Sliver, all of which were made into films. Along with these he also wrote the long-running Broadway comic thriller Deathtrap. All of which makes me wonder why I’d left it so long to sample his work.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12279023.A_Kiss_Before_Dying" title="A Kiss Before Dying by Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kiss Before Dying</a> (1953), his first novel, is a taut and tense suspense novel. It reminded me of Patricia Highsmith’s The Talented Mr Ripley, which it predates by a year. It really stands up too and does not feel remotely dated. The novel switches viewpoints, most memorably between cold blooded killer and victim. There are a couple of clever twists and the whole thing is so gripping and perfectly realised that it would be easy to read in one sitting.<br><br>I look forward to more <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin" title="Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ira Levin</a><br><br>4/5<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1475928584l/12279023._SY475_.jpg" width="180" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12279023.A_Kiss_Before_Dying" title="A Kiss Before Dying by Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kiss Before Dying</a> not only debuted the talent of best-selling novelist <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8050.Ira_Levin" title="Ira Levin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ira Levin</a> to rave reviews, it also set a new standard in the art of mystery and suspense. <br><br>Now a modern classic, as gripping in its tautly plotted action as it is penetrating in its exploration of a criminal mind, it tells the shocking tale of a young man who will stop at nothing--not even murder--to get where he wants to go. For he has dreams; plans. He also has charm, good looks, sex appeal, intelligence. And he has a problem. Her name is Dorothy; she loves him, and she's pregnant. The solution may demand desperate measures. But, then, he looks like the kind of guy who could get away with murder. Compellingly, step by determined step, the novel follows this young man in his execution of one plan he had neither dreamed nor foreseen. Nor does he foresee how inexorably he will be enmeshed in the consequences of his own extreme deed.</i><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16923834575100254348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_994059741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994059741" />
    <a title="Realini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7873218-realini"><img alt="Realini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420269105p2/7873218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994059741?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Realini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Realini" href="/user/show/7873218-realini">Realini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7873218-realini?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994059741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer498630916985565373">A Kiss Before Dying by Ira Levin<br/><br/>I stay away from detective stories. Even this excellent book was a near miss- I have read a few pages and was on the point of abandoning it. I tend to put away books quite quickly, a fault which is destined to make place for a second run of the books I admire, in case I run out of new books that I like. Since I know that I have some 70-80 books that not only I love, but with time I will forget much of their plot and events, what is the point to hang on to works th</span>
  <span id="freeText498630916985565373" style="display:none">A Kiss Before Dying by Ira Levin<br /><br />I stay away from detective stories. Even this excellent book was a near miss- I have read a few pages and was on the point of abandoning it. I tend to put away books quite quickly, a fault which is destined to make place for a second run of the books I admire, in case I run out of new books that I like. Since I know that I have some 70-80 books that not only I love, but with time I will forget much of their plot and events, what is the point to hang on to works that seem indigestible?<br />Well, A Kiss Before Dying offers an answer.<br />There were two options: one- after reading two pages and looking on the cover and seeing this is a crime story, I could put it away, second: try and stick a while with it.<br />It paid off handsomely- not only I got trapped and enticed by this thrilling book, but I loved it so much that I offered it to myself in small portions, like caviar.<br />Now the problem is- how do I tell you about it?<br />Since there is no question of mentioning something of the plot, I am thinking of the start. From the start we get “action’- violence is present to begin with.<br />This in fact my main opposition to the crime stories:<br />-why waste time reading about a guy (the killer is rarely a woman, if I am not mistaken) who is violent, devious and unworthy??<br />- perhaps for same reason that we read about Mephisto, Machiavelli, Wormwood…these people or demons exist and sometimes they make for pretty interesting personages<br />- it is often more exciting to learn about characters that are complex, smart, but also devilish, than have one-sided and often boring roles.<br /><br />The Smartest Guy in the Room is the author. It takes gumption to create such complex stories with surprising, if not shocking events.<br />The perspective of Ira Levin is flawless. At one point, there is a new apparition that I thought will stay with us for a while, if not to the end. <br />Unlike the blockbuster movies where you figure out from the start- this is a star who gets $ twenty million per movies, so he or she is going to hang around to the end and survive aliens, tornadoes, tsunamis, you name it. There is a slim chance that he only got two million for that role and then he may disappear after ten minutes, but it is a long shot, with odds of one to twenty.<br />There is a feel of “too much” in A Kiss Before Dying, I can’t say from what angle, since I am sworn to not give anything away, but even that aspect is amazingly handled by Ira Levin, who is a master of dealing with suspense and making you believe things are really turning out the way you read about them.<br />The psychological insight of such a great author is nothing short of marvelous. The creepy thing is you start wondering:<br />- Is this guy for real, or what?<br />- It looks like Levin has all it takes to kill someone<br />- but what if he did? He is so good at planning everything; he will get away with it.<br />Kevorkian, the Literature professor I had in high school used to say that every masterpiece has an excellent crime story in it. I am thinking Crime and Punishment, War and Peace …But what is the crime story in Madame Bovary? Perhaps her infidelity?<br /><br />This is an excellent book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="498630916985565373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9515486038197923994">This is the story of what happens when a girl gets pregnant and the boy will do whatever he can to make sure she's not a burden on him.<br/><br/>Boys will do anything for the nookie. And money.<br/><br/>I recently watched the 1956 movie based on this book, the one with Robert Wagner and Joanne Woodward, the one I had never connected to this book. I watched it anyway but picked up the book from the library afterwards, thinking there might be some differences. There really weren't any. What you see in the movie is al</span>
  <span id="freeText9515486038197923994" style="display:none">This is the story of what happens when a girl gets pregnant and the boy will do whatever he can to make sure she's not a burden on him.<br /><br />Boys will do anything for the nookie. And money.<br /><br />I recently watched the 1956 movie based on this book, the one with Robert Wagner and Joanne Woodward, the one I had never connected to this book. I watched it anyway but picked up the book from the library afterwards, thinking there might be some differences. There really weren't any. What you see in the movie is almost exactly the same as the book. The few differences were probably made out of ease of filming or casting, though there was the addition of Joanne Woodward taking a awkward topple off a set of bleachers in the movie that didn't show up in the book. I don't know why, but I really hoped that scene would be in the book. Primarily because the scene in the movie was really strange.<br /><br />Also: Robert Wagner is creepy. Even before his possible hand in the death of Natalie Wood years later, Wagner did creepy like no one's bidness.<br /><br />This is a quick read, one recommended for anyone who likes reading thrillers. I didn't think I'd get through it in pretty much one sitting, but I did. And, again, watching the movie first didn't really spoil anything for me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2877245814730557583">I liked this book very much because it's so clever, so carefully constructed, but it also made me terribly sad. Oh, about human beings and trust between them, you know. Whom do you trust, that is the question. I remember how my parents were dead keen to persuade me not to marry that man (and he was certainly not a murderer) but that only strengthened my resolve to go ahead and marry. Once you love somebody, you are blind. And it is possible indeed that if you put in a lot of work, you can make a</span>
  <span id="freeText2877245814730557583" style="display:none">I liked this book very much because it's so clever, so carefully constructed, but it also made me terribly sad. Oh, about human beings and trust between them, you know. Whom do you trust, that is the question. I remember how my parents were dead keen to persuade me not to marry that man (and he was certainly not a murderer) but that only strengthened my resolve to go ahead and marry. Once you love somebody, you are blind. And it is possible indeed that if you put in a lot of work, you can make a person fall in love with you. Newspapers are full of stories of con men and worse, some evidently very successful, even online.<br />As a novel, I can't fault it, even envy it a bit. It's the kind of book I wish I had written. Except I am not a thriller writer and quite often I think that thrillers as a genre are really not for me. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630315398?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Pageant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Pageant" href="/user/show/25561549-nick-pageant">Nick Pageant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25561549-nick-pageant?shelf=gen-fic">gen-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630315398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4942282669200350126">This was just deliciously trashy. I loved every page and can't believe how well it has aged. It's one of those rare finds - a literary novel with a pulp sensibility. Great fun. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17285850378712394463">Classic and nearly 5 stars until Part 3. The overwrought dramatically staged ending somehow dated the plot as much as it also diminished the onion-like layers of duplicitous evil / perp's self identity exposing. This copy had a worthy Introduction that I also enjoyed. This was his debut work. Also probably his best.</span>

<div id="review_436548397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436548397" />
    <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez"><img alt="Anthony Chavez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314570438p2/4876333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436548397?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Chavez" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez">Anthony Chavez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780762102518" href="/book/show/2396316.A_Kiss_Before_Dying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876333-anthony-chavez?shelf=the-classics">the-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436548397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14895013195097712604">I felt as though Ira Levin really got into the characters' heads, especially reformed party-girl Ellen and spinster-in-training Marion, although it could be that their relative depth was a relief after lovestruck wannabe-wed Dorothy. The novel was peppered with newspaper items relating to the various crimes of the story. They were all pretty tongue-in-cheek and served as nice palate-cleansers between the point of view changes. The thing that sets this book apart from other, similarly plotted sus</span>
  <span id="freeText14895013195097712604" style="display:none">I felt as though Ira Levin really got into the characters' heads, especially reformed party-girl Ellen and spinster-in-training Marion, although it could be that their relative depth was a relief after lovestruck wannabe-wed Dorothy. The novel was peppered with newspaper items relating to the various crimes of the story. They were all pretty tongue-in-cheek and served as nice palate-cleansers between the point of view changes. The thing that sets this book apart from other, similarly plotted suspense stories is the way that Levin plays with our emotions concerning the murderer. For the first third of the novel, there is a small part of us that is sympathetic with this man; we almost catch ourselves hoping that he doesn't get caught, I mean he worked so hard to marry money I felt like he deserved it. Several surprises later, however, and our emotions are totally flip-flopped. Now we are given information from another perspective, and we can see just how monstrous this man really is.<br /><br />The dialogue is so natural and easy. I wonder if some of it ended up in the film, which I will now permit myself to see. The women in the novel are lively enough but I just wished that one of them didn't need a male protector; However, this was written in the 1950s, and I need to remind myself of that. The mind of the hero/villain though is convincingly done and the overall plot makes this one a real page-turner. An excellent guilty pleasure. 4-stars indeed. I definitely want to read "Rosemary's Baby" and "The Stepford Wives" now.<br /><br />If your into the hard boiled crime genre definitely pick this up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14895013195097712604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pHURcabSzjCrrluOpaZSWld+vFLwDtXM43uXexe1g/dnTdV6+9gEeV0op7TbtHhdGInylzIUmOSb46TpAnnfWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8pt2x4V+62Odu+zAKqCr58zIxXQ7cim/u8/oIHNGJosxo7LM2HQhKms9EPpUsoHggz+LsfloZJfDV9uyZop6JQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15229851503097884093">Levin graduated from the Horace Mann School and New York University, where he majored in philosophy and English.<br/><br/>After college, he wrote training films and scripts for television.<br/><br/>Levin's first produced play was <i>No Time for Sergeants</i> (adapted from Mac Hyman's novel), a comedy about a hillbilly drafted into the United States Air Force that launched the career of Andy Griffith. The play was turned int</span>
  <span id="freeText15229851503097884093" style="display:none">Levin graduated from the Horace Mann School and New York University, where he majored in philosophy and English.<br /><br />After college, he wrote training films and scripts for television.<br /><br />Levin's first produced play was <i>No Time for Sergeants</i> (adapted from Mac Hyman's novel), a comedy about a hillbilly drafted into the United States Air Force that launched the career of Andy Griffith. The play was turned into a movie in 1958, and co-starred Don Knotts, Griffith's long-time co-star and friend. <i>No Time for Sergeants</i> is generally considered the precursor to <i>Gomer Pyle, USMC</i>. <br /><br />Levin's first novel,<i> A Kiss Before Dying</i>, was well received, earning him the 1954 Edgar Award for Best First Novel. <i>A Kiss Before Dying</i> was turned into a movie twice, first in 1956, and again in 1991.<br /><br />Levin's best known play is <i>Deathtrap</i>, which holds the record as the longest-running comedy-thriller on Broadway and brought Levin his second Edgar Award. In 1982, it was made into a film starring Christopher Reeve and Michael Caine.<br /><br />Levin's best known novel is <i>Rosemary's Baby</i>, a horror story of modern day satanism and the occult, set in Manhattan's Upper West Side. It was made into a film starring Mia Farrow and John Cassavetes. Ruth Gordon won an Oscar for Best Actress in a Supporting Role for her performance. Roman Polanski, who wrote and directed the film, was nominated for Best Writing, Screenplay Based on Material from Another Medium.<br /><br />Other Levin novels were turned into movies, including <i>The Boys from Brazil</i> in 1978; <i>The Stepford Wives</i> in 1975 and again in 2004; and <i>Sliver</i> in 1993. <br /><br />Stephen King has described Ira Levin as "the Swiss watchmaker of suspense novels, he makes what the rest of us do look like cheap watchmakers in drugstores." Chuck Palahniuk, in , calls Levin's writing "a smart, updated version of the kind of folksy legends that cultures have always used."<br /><br />Ira Levin died from a heart attack at his home in Manhattan, on 12 November 2007. He was seventy-eight at the time of his death.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15229851503097884093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
